I want to self-host jikan v4 from my Render free account and MongoDB for storing the scraped data from myanimelist. I forked the Jikan GitHub into my GitHub. You can use my forked jikan. I want jikan v4 all (endpoints/parameters/pagination/filters) exactly the same as jikan v4 official endpoints.
01. First, the main root endpoint that have entire myanimelist animes "/v4/anime?page={page_number&limit=25&sfw=true" by default adds a hentai filter, so it does not scrape hentai from MyAnimeList. I use the hentai filter parameter or not. It would return per page max 25 animes to the last page. Anime should be ordered by MAL ID, low to high MAL ID, like the official "/anime" endpoint. I can go through the paginated pages (last visible page - current page - has next page - total pages - per page anime limit {based on the limit in endpoint url}). All anime listing, supports status, type, order_by, sort. start_from. The "anime" root endpoint should scrape all the anime from MyAnimeList like the jikan v4 official and spread across paginated pages. Collection will grow with MyAnimeList adding new anime to their site. Default ordering will be lower mal id to higher mal id, exactly the jikan "/anime" endpoint.
last_visible_page = {last_visible_page_number} → The final page number available. IN my self-hosted jikan v4, make sure the paginated pages do not have duplicates scrapped data like jikan has with their paginated pages. I do not want my self-hosted jikan v4. Any endpoint paginated page has duplicate anime data.

has_next_page = true → There is a next page of results (you're not on the last page)

current_page = x (e.g., 1) → You're currently viewing page 1

items.count = 25 → Number of results returned on this page

items.total = {total_number_of_animes_data} (e.g., 30371) → Total number of results available across all pages

items.per_page = 25 → Maximum results per page (the max limit can be set)

Root "/anime" endpoints:

Main Root anime endpoint with status and hentai filter: "https://api.jikan.moe/v4/anime?sfw=true&page={page_number}&limit=25" When I use this endpoint from my self-host it should return exact JSON data like the official Jikan v4. This is the main endpoint for searching and retrieving lists of anime data from MyAnimeList. It's the main root anime endpoint where all anime data is shown. All means all. Myanimelist all anime plus future ones as well when myanimelist gonna add then into their site. All myanimelist scraped anime will be spread across paginated pages and by default ordered from lower MAL ID to higher MAL ID. 

Root anime endpoint with status and hentai filter: "https://api.jikan.moe/v4/seasons/now?sfw=true&page={page_number}&limit=25" When I use this endpoint from my self-host it should return exact JSON data like jikan v4. All myanimelist top airing anime data is spread across pagination pages. 

Sub root "/anime' endpoints:
Top-Ranking Anime (by Score)
This returns anime ranked by their MyAnimeList score.

Endpoint: /top/anime

Default Behaviour: Returns the top-ranked list by score.

Example:
https://api.jikan.moe/v4/top/anime?sfw=true&page={page_number}&limit=25 -> the endpoint should return all top airing anime it scraped from MyAnimeList and spread across paginated pages. 

Most Popular Anime
This returns anime ranked by the number of members on MyAnimeList.

Endpoint: /top/anime

Filter Parameter: filter=bypopularity

Example:
https://api.jikan.moe/v4/top/anime?filter=bypopularity&sfw=true&page={page_number}&limit=25 -> the endpoint should return all top anime by popularity anime it scraped from MyAnimeList and spread across paginated pages.

Most Favourited Anime
This returns anime ranked by the number of times they've been added to users' favorites lists.

Endpoint: /top/anime

Filter Parameter: filter=favorite

Example:
https://api.jikan.moe/v4/top/anime?filter=favorite&sfw=true&page=1&limit=25 -> the endpoint should return all top anime by favourite anime it scraped from MyAnimeList and spread across paginated pages.
] 

I want the continuing parameter to be specifically used with Season endpoints to include long-running anime that started in a previous season but are still airing.
How to Use It
You add &continuing=true to the URL of a season endpoint to include these continuing shows in the results.

Here are examples of the endpoints:

Currently Airing (/seasons/now):
https://api.jikan.moe/v4/seasons/now?sfw=true&continuing=true&page={page-number}&limit=25 -> scraped all anime related to this endpoint from MyAnimeList and spread across all paginated pages.

Upcoming Anime (/seasons/upcoming):
https://api.jikan.moe/v4/seasons/upcoming?sfw=true&continuing=true&page={page_number}&limit=25 -> scraped all anime related to this endpoint from MyAnimeList and spread across all paginated pages.

I also want so I can use it with other season endpoints too, like a specific season (/seasons/{year}/{season}

Important Notes:
It's a boolean: Its value is either true or false. Omitting it is the same as false.

Endpoint limitation: The continuing parameter only works with season endpoints (/seasons/now, /seasons/upcoming, /seasons/{year}/{season}), not with the general /anime search endpoint.

Known behaviour: Including continuing=true might return anime that don't strictly belong to that season. This is a known behaviour of the API

Satellite channel WOWOW picked up the series in the fall of that year and aired it in its entirety uncensored. Cowboy Bebop was not a ratings hit in Japan, but sold over 19,000 DVD units in the initial release run, and 81,000 overall. Protagonist Spike Spiegel won Best Male Character, and Megumi Hayashibara won Best Voice Actor for her role as Faye Valentine in the 1999 and 2000 Anime Grand Prix, respectively. Cowboy Bebop's biggest influence has been in the United States, where it premiered on Adult Swim in 2001 with many reruns since. The show's heavy Western influence struck a chord with American viewers, where it became a \"gateway drug\" to anime aimed at adult audiences.",

The initial Geneon Entertainment USA (then known as Pioneer) releases on VHS and DVD (singles, Signature Series, and box set) used only the first opening on each episode. This was due to the Japanese licensor providing them clean materials for only the first opening to put the English credits on. When FUNimation Entertainment picked up the show in 2010 and released it, they repeated Geneon's mistake of using only the first opening on every episode. This mistake was later fixed in 2013 on the Anime Classics re-release.",

      "background": "The anime had a hiatus from October 13, 2024, to April 6, 2025. The anime switched to a seasonal release model starting from April 5, 2026. The airing time was Wednesdays 19:00 between October 20, 1999 - March 2001. The airing time was changed to Sundays 19:30 between April 2001 - December 2004. The airing time was changed to Sundays 9:30 between October 6, 2006 - October 13, 2024. The airing time was again changed to Sundays 23:15 on April 6, 2025. Several anime-original arcs have been adapted into light novels, and the series has inspired 50+ video games as of 2023. In June 2004, One Piece was licensed in North America by 4Kids Entertainment, which partnered with Viz Media for home video distribution. As One Piece proved unsuitable for their target demographic, 4Kids Entertainment censored the show to meet their standards, and, in December 2006, they stopped its production. In April 2007, Funimation took over the series licensing, providing an uncut version that remained faithful to the original release. In Japan, the anime's first 574 episodes were released exclusively on DVD by Avex Pictures from February 21, 2001, to December 4, 2013. Blu-rays also became available with the DVDs starting on January 8, 2014. In North America, Viz Media released the anime on DVD between February 28, 2006, and June 26, 2007. Funimation has re-released and continued the series since May 27, 2008. From March 23, 2021, the DVDs were accompanied by Blu-rays as well.",

      "background": "Trinity Blood premiered in Japan on the satellite network WOWOW on April 28, 2005 and ran until October 6, 2005. The satellite channel Animax also aired the series across its networks. The Funimation English dubbing of the series premiered on Canadian television on the Razer network on July 6, 2006; and in the United States as part of Cartoon Network's Adult Swim block on September 9, 2006. The series enjoyed strong television ratings when it originally aired in Japan. Its North American debut was also considered successful; it is credited for being one of four Funimation properties that helped the company achieve a 47.8% sales gain in 2006. Funimation gave Trinity Blood a 90-minute US theatrical release to promote the series. The film, titled Trinity Blood: Genesis, is a compilation of the first four episodes of the series and released on May 5, 2006 in conjunction with Anime Central in Chicago, IL.",

      "background": "Director Hideaki Anno's depression is what led to the dark themes of Shinseiki Evangelion. Budgetary problems and parental complaints about content led to the original ending being scrapped and replaced with an extremely limited-animation ending breaking from the main plot. A movie, Air/Magokoro wo, Kimi ni, was later made based in part on the original planned ending and in part on Anno's increasing frustration with the otaku fanbase. The series' mix of psychoanalysis, religious symbolism, and genre deconstruction proved extremely influential on mature anime in the late '90s onward. The Japan Media Arts Festival in 2006 ranked it as the most popular anime of all time.",

      "background": "Mamoru Oshii's Ghost in the Shell was the first film to adapt Masamune Shirow's manga of the same name. It heavily condenses the original storyline, reducing the original material's comic relief and sexual content in favor of a more serious tone and changing the setting from Japan to a city modelled after Hong Kong. The artwork within the animated film was produced using an innovative mix of cel animation and digital effects. Ghost in the Shell is one of the world's most famous Japanese animated films, being the first to reach #1 on Billboard magazine's video best-seller list, and also served as a major inspiration for the Wachowskis in their creation of the Matrix movies. A special edition titled Ghost in the Shell: 2.0 was released in 2008, which features scenes reanimated with additional CGI to match the style of the 2004's sequel, Ghost in the Shell: Innocence.",

The recommendation "https://api.jikan.moe/v4/anime/{mal_id}/recommendations" endpoint is the same as the Jikan v4 official endpoint for a specific anime. Based on that specific anime, it will scrape all the recommended anime users recommended in MyAnimeList. Scraped the full entire recomendations data from MyAnimeList for a specific anime. If all recommended anime scraped more than 25, then apply pagination on the endpoint. Do not miss a single anime data. I want the response to look exactly like this:

____________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________

I also want the jikan v4 official "https://api.jikan.moe/v4/schedules?day=friday&sfw=true&page={page_number&limit=25" endpoint in my jikan v4 version as well. When will I use the schedule endpoint with "day" filter, it should return all the "currently airing" status anime. Returns a list of currently airing anime, organized by their broadcast day.
>  How to Filter by Day: 
Filter the schedule by adding the day parameter to the request. The accepted values for the day parameter are the days of the week in lowercase:

monday

tuesday

wednesday

thursday

friday

saturday

sunday

There are also two special values in the request that can be used:

other: For anime that don't have a specific broadcast day.

unknown: For anime where the broadcast day is not known

> Example Requests
Here is how you would structure the requests for each day

To get the schedule for Friday, filtered to exclude adult content, and with pagination: "https://api.jikan.moe/v4/schedules?day={day_name}&sfw=true&page={page_number&limit=25"

> Other Useful Parameters:
So, I can combine the day filter with other common Jikan parameters:

01. sfw (boolean): Set to true to filter out adult (hentai) content.

02. page (integer): Specifies the page number of results.

03. limit (integer): Specifies the number of results per page (the maximum is usually 25).

04. filter (string): Filter the results by anime type (e.g., tv, movie, ova, special).

05. kids (boolean): Filter to include only anime for kids

______________________________________________________________________________________________________________________

To scrape anime by filters like **type**, **season/year**, **genre**, **theme**, **demographic**, or **studio**, use Jikan v4's `/anime` search endpoint** with specific query parameters. Some filters use IDs while others use simple string values.

Here’s a practical guide for each filter.

---

### 1. By Type, Season, Year, and Studio

These use straightforward query parameters on the `/anime` endpoint.

| Filter | Parameter | Value Example | Example URL |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Type** | `type` | `tv`, `movie`, `ova`, `ona`, `special`, `music` | `/v4/anime?type=tv&sfw=true` |
| **Season** | `season` | `winter`, `spring`, `summer`, `fall` | `/v4/anime?season=summer&year=2024&sfw=true` |
| **Year** | `start_date` / `end_date` | `YYYY-MM-DD` | `/v4/anime?start_date=2024-01-01&end_date=2024-12-31&sfw=true` |
| **Studio** | `producers` | Studio ID (e.g., `1` for Sunrise) | `/v4/anime?producers=1&sfw=true` |

**Notes:**
*   The `type` parameter filters by the anime's format.
*   For **season** and **year**, I can use the `season` and `year` parameters together (e.g., `?season=summer&year=2024`) or separately, both ways. For a date range, use `start_date` and `end_date`.
*   `producers` actually refers to **studios** and producers. 

---

### 2. By Genre, Theme, and Demographic

These filters also use the `/anime` endpoint, but they require **numeric IDs** that you must fetch first from the `/genres/anime` endpoint.

**Step 1: Get the ID for your filter.**

Call the genres endpoint to get a list of all genres, themes, and demographics with their IDs.

```
GET /v4/genres/anime
```

> Step 2: Use the ID in your search.

Once I have the ID, I can use it with the `genres` parameter on the `/anime` endpoint.

| Filter | Parameter | Value | Example URL |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Genre** | `genres` | ID(s) comma-separated | `/v4/anime?genres=1,2&sfw=true` (Action & Adventure) |
| **Theme** | `genres` | ID(s) comma-separated | `/v4/anime?genres=39&sfw=true` (for "Military" theme) |
| **Demographic** | `genres` | ID(s) comma-separated | `/v4/anime?genres=27&sfw=true` (for "Shounen" demographic) |

**Important Notes:**
*   Genres, themes, and demographics are all returned from the `/genres/anime` endpoint and are all filtered using the **same `genres` parameter**.
*   You can combine multiple IDs with commas (e.g., `genres=1,2,3`).
*   To **exclude** certain genres, use the `genres_exclude` parameter.

---

> Common Parameters for All Searches

You can add these to any of the above requests:

| Parameter | Description |
| :--- | :--- |
| `sfw=true` | **Essential** – Filters out adult/hentai content |
| `page` | Page number for pagination |
| `limit` | Results per page (max 25) |
| `order_by` | Sort by `score`, `popularity`, `title`, `start_date`, etc. |
| `sort` | `desc` (default) or `asc` |

> Quick Reference Table

| What You Want | Endpoint & Parameters | Example |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **By Type** (TV) | `/anime?type=tv` | `/v4/anime?type=tv&sfw=true&limit=25` |
| **By Season/Year** | `/anime?season=summer&year=2024` | `/v4/anime?season=summer&year=2024&sfw=true` |
| **By Year Range** | `/anime?start_date=YYYY-MM-DD&end_date=YYYY-MM-DD` | `/v4/anime?start_date=2024-01-01&end_date=2024-12-31&sfw=true` |
| **By Studio** | `/anime?producers={studio_id}` | `/v4/anime?producers=1&sfw=true` |
| **By Genre/Theme/Demographic** | `/anime?genres={id}` | `/v4/anime?genres=1,2&sfw=true` |
| **Get All Genre IDs** | `/genres/anime` | `/v4/genres/anime` |

> Pro Tip: Combining Filters

You can combine multiple filters in one request. For example, to get **TV anime from Summer 2024 that are Action or Adventure and SFW**:

```
/v4/anime?type=tv&season=summer&year=2024&genres=1,2&sfw=true&page=1&limit=25

```

This approach will give me full flexibility to build complex queries.
